## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t, which is the fundamental problem in chemical kinetics. The rate law typically depends on powers of concentration, but time-dependent forcing or catalyst deactivation can introduce explicit time dependence.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction with single species)
- General n-th order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (power-law rate law)
- Mixed order / Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (surface-catalyzed reaction with saturation)
- Second-order Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 / (c1 + A)**2 (dual-site surface reaction)
- Autocatalytic with decay: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order terms)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (catalyst deactivation or activation over time)
- Fractional order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with constant source/sink)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction approaching equilibrium)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) + c2 * A (enzymatic with additional linear term)
- Power-law with time modulation: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (time-dependent rate coefficient)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type cooperative binding)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear dependence of rate on concentration → first-order kinetics (dA_dt = c*A), characteristic of unimolecular reactions
- Quadratic dependence on concentration → second-order kinetics, characteristic of bimolecular collisions between identical species
- Rate that plateaus at high concentration → Michaelis-Menten or Langmuir-Hinshelwood saturation mechanism with denominator (c + A)
- Rate that peaks then decreases with increasing A → substrate inhibition, modeled by A/(c + A**2) or similar rational forms
- Explicit time dependence in rate law → non-elementary process such as catalyst deactivation, photolysis with varying light, or sequential mechanism with intermediates
- Negative rate values (dA_dt < 0) → consumption/decay reaction; positive values → production or autocatalysis
- Sum of two power-law terms in A → parallel reaction pathways with different molecularities
- Rate proportional to A*(c0 - A) → logistic-type autocatalytic reaction where product catalyzes its own formation from finite substrate
